Difference in property: -1.159 - 0.248 = -1.407

From 5 to 8 carbons: 3 carbons * -0.2814 = -0.8442

Ethyl benzoate combines an aromatic ring (which might push the value more negative) with an ester group (which might moderate the value toward zero or slightly negative). Comparing to CCOC(=O)c1ccccc1S(=O)(=O)NN(C=O)c2nc(Cl)cc(OC)n2 (1.39067613), which has additional polar and complex groups leading to a positive value, I expect ethyl benzoate to have a less positive or slightly negative value due to the absence of such polar substituents.

### Step 4: Estimate the Property Value
- The aromatic ring in ethyl benzoate suggests a tendency toward negative values, as seen in many benzene-containing compounds.
- The ester group, as seen in aliphatic esters like CCCCC(=O)OCC (-0.84471038), also suggests a value around -0.8.
- Since ethyl benzoate is simpler and less polar than the substituted ethyl benzoate derivative (1.39067613), its value should be lower (more negative).

Balancing these observations, I predict the property value for ethyl benzoate to be in the range of aliphatic esters but slightly more negative due to the aromatic ring. A reasonable estimate, considering the values of similar compounds, is around -0.7 to -0.9.

### Final Prediction
Based on the structural analysis and comparison with similar molecules, I predict the property value for CCOC(=O)c1ccccc1 (ethyl benzoate) to be approximately **-0.75**.
